  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_63cb0e62-67e0-4d3d-ac5e-899a5e0ac4f6'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer3854646648562952301">With <i>Pandora</i>, Anne Rice began a magnificent new series of vampire novels. Now, in the second of her New Tales of the Vampires, she tells the mesmerizing story of Vittorio, a vampire in the Italian Age of Gold.<br/><br/>Educated in the Florence of Cosimo de' Medici, trained in knighthood at his father's mountaintop castle, Vittorio inhabits a world of courtly splendor and country ple</span>
  <span id="freeText3854646648562952301" style="display:none">With <i>Pandora</i>, Anne Rice began a magnificent new series of vampire novels. Now, in the second of her New Tales of the Vampires, she tells the mesmerizing story of Vittorio, a vampire in the Italian Age of Gold.<br /><br />Educated in the Florence of Cosimo de' Medici, trained in knighthood at his father's mountaintop castle, Vittorio inhabits a world of courtly splendor and country pleasures - a world suddenly threatened when his entire family is confronted by an unholy power.<br /><br />In the midst of this upheaval, Vittorio is seduced by the vampire Ursula, the most beautiful of his supernatural enemies. As he sets out in pursuit of vengeance, entering the nightmarish Court of the Ruby Grail, increasingly more enchanted (and confused) by his love for the mysterious Ursula, he finds himself facing demonic adversaries, war and political intrigue.<br /><br />Against a backdrop of the wonders - both sacred and profane - and the beauty and ferocity of Renaissance Italy, Anne Rice creates a passionate and tragic legend of doomed young love and lost innocence.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3854646648562952301" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="bookReviews">
  




  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1129451812" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1129451812" />
    <a title="Rinoa Heartilly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1946963-rinoa-heartilly"><img alt="Rinoa Heartilly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456093630p2/1946963.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1129451812?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rinoa Heartilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rinoa Heartilly" href="/user/show/1946963-rinoa-heartilly">Rinoa Heartilly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1946963-rinoa-heartilly?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1129451812" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4125846359203852560">-- contains spoilers --<br/><br/>Okay, so here's the thing. <br/><i>Interview with the Vampire</i>, Rice's debut novel and at the same time the first novel in the now two-digit numbered <i>Chronicles of the vampires</i> series, was published in 1976, but written in 1973, following the tragic passing away of Rice's young daughter Michele of leukemia in 1972. It has since then gone on to become an international bestseller and literary classic even outside of its genre, as well as being an integral part in founding a new under</span>
  <span id="freeText4125846359203852560" style="display:none">-- contains spoilers --<br /><br />Okay, so here's the thing. <br /><i>Interview with the Vampire</i>, Rice's debut novel and at the same time the first novel in the now two-digit numbered <i>Chronicles of the vampires</i> series, was published in 1976, but written in 1973, following the tragic passing away of Rice's young daughter Michele of leukemia in 1972. It has since then gone on to become an international bestseller and literary classic even outside of its genre, as well as being an integral part in founding a new understanding of the vampire myth. It's largely regarded as Rice's magnum opus and though it's not my favourite novel of hers (that would be <i>The Vampire Armand</i> due to an excessive case of nostalgia), I agree that it is her best. This is partly due to how tightly <i>Interview</i> is tied to Rice's personal life and how genuine all of what it presents therefore is.<br /><br />Rice suffered from depression after the traumatic death of her daughter and turned to rewriting an old short story of hers. <i>Interview</i> is clearly very much rooted in Rice's own emotional situation, with poor Claudia, the little girl that was never going to live, and the emotional rift and absence of mutual understanding between her parents, Louis and Lestat, with Louis feeling perpetually resentful and wary to the point of incomprehension of his sire. This is of course a direct connection to the reality of Anne and Stan Rice's marital situation and a common occurence in a couple who lost their child. Rice has admitted to her husband being the inspiration behind Lestat and the picture <i>Interview</i> paints of him is not a very fond one. Lestat is in a way the villain of the majority of <i>Interview</i>.<br /><br />Fast-forward several years, to 1985 and the publication in the second book of the <i>Chronicles</i>, <i>The Vampire Lestat</i>. As one might gleam from the title, it is Lestat's turn to tell his tale now and boy do the contradictions pile up. Lestat/Rice excuses most of his behaviour in <i>Interview</i> by either giving background information that undermines Louis' impressions or flat out denying certain events even happened. Lestat developes into the lovable, fun, childish little rascal we all know and love™ and that he would continue to portray in the following books.<br /><br /><i>Audible and overly dramatic sigh here.</i><br /><br />See, this right here is one of the central problems of the <i>Chronicles</i> and the reason reading half of it <b>
  <i>pisses the shit out of me</i>
</b>. Rice relies here on the principle of the unreliable narrator which, you know? Fine. I'm not opposed to Louis maybe getting some things wrong and of course there is always the fact that different viewpoints will inevitably end up with different conclusions. The problem is just <i>how much</i> she takes advantage of it. <i>The Vampire Lestat</i> absolves the titular character of basically every single thing and it's fucking <i>cheap</i>. <i>Interview</i> loses at least half of its impact knowing the contants of <i>Lestat</i>. <br /><br />Anne and Stan Rice ended up being married for 41 years, right up to Stan's death, so things between them had obviously improved after <i>Interview</i>, especially with the birth of their son Christopher in 1978. <i>Lestat</i> was written by a much happier Anne Rice than <i>Interview</i> was. And that is of course wonderful and I am genuinely happy for them. However, it also means that Lestat, being based on Stan as mentioned, underwent a <i>huge</i> and very much canon-breaking change of character in what kind of reads like Rice retroactively apologizing to her husband for the less than fond portrayal in <i>Interview</i>.<br /><br />The problem with this is a simple fact - Lestat, despite being based on him, is <i>not</i> Stan Rice. He is a fictional creation, bound to an established world and character and the fact that the Rice's marriage was improving does not mean that what Anne Rice wrote in <i>Interview</i> is somehow less valid. Despite it being a key factor to <i>Interview's</i> overall success, reality robbed <i>Lestat</i> and the character in itself in the following books of authenticity. Which is why I kind of really dislike the character now lol.<br /><br />Okay, so what exactly does this have to do with <i>Vittorio</i>, a book centering around a vampire that has never interacted with the main cast? Look up. See those four stars? Yes, I actually really enjoyed <i>Vittorio</i>, despite it being seemingly mostly despised by other people. Why? Well, I actually truly believe Rice has a great talent for portraying the desperation of being and provoking thought and <i>Vittorio</i> is a <i>great</i> example for this. Vittorio is the only vampire in the entirety of the <i>Chronicles</i> that I can think of who actually has time to struggle with the idea of what it means to become immortal, to have knowledge of your impending rebirth and to have that pain be inflicted by someone he loved, protected, <i>trusted</i> (except for David but we never get his perspective on things and he gets over it in like a second) and when he knows he's done for he fucking <i>despises</i> it. I liked Vittorio as a character. He's brash, fervent, entirely believable as a teenager and not actually very smart. I also like that 95 % of this book chronicles the last week of his human life, mostly taking up by him thinking about revenge and exacting said revenge against the vampires who killed his family. It's different, fresh. We don't actually see anything of his 500 years of being a vampire because his humanity is so much more important to him. In a way <i>Vittorio</i> is not actually about vampires at all, rather the radiance of human life (haha, get it? If not read the book).<br /><br />Vittorio ends up with both the girl and immortality and he is <i>miserable</i>. The book ends like this. And Vittorio actually lets Ursula <i>survive</i>, stays with her and is still with her in the present, a fact I found remarkably surprising because the book had me so convinced he was going to kill her. Their companionship is also probably one of if not the most longlasting in the entire series? Again, Vittorio breaks out of by now well known patterns of the <i>Chronicles</i>.<br /><br />All of this would not have worked as well had the character of Ursula not been as compelling as she turned out to be and therefore Vittorio falling for her not been as convincing. The central axis of the tale hinges upon the one scene where he can't bring himself to kill her defenseless self because of his firm belief in the existence of her soul (he turns out to be right) and it is this so altruistic belief which initiates his ultimate fall. Real kudos to Rice here because she managed to get me very invested in Ursula's plight, despite the minimal amount of screentime she has. Especially fascinating to follow was the process of her unravelling, going from the initial fearsome and highly erotic monster to her reveal as a basically clue- and helpless 200-year-old little girl. Even when human Vittorio turns out to be the dominant part of the couple. The power play aspect of their relationship makes it one of the more remarkable of the series.<br /><br />There is of course stuff that I wasn't too fond of as well, such as the cardboard cutout characters of the other vampires and the weird pseudo-rape somehere near the beginning of the book as well as the ever popular 'Hey, you have never heard of me but I totally exist and I'm super powerful too lol!' (you gotta ask yourself just <i>how many</i> vampires Akasha just simply forgot), but these ultimately did not impact my enjoyment of the book very much. The subject of faith and heavenly beings is also handled a lot better than in the <b>
  <i>god awful</i>
</b> <i>Memnoch the Devil</i> because it is less of a 'Surprise! The Devil and God are real and Lestat was at the Crucifixion of Christ!' punch in the stomach and more of a quiet introduction of a concept that you also have the choice to write off as Vittorio's hallucinations.<br /><br />Okay to summarize, fuck Lestat's sudden 180° change of character and fuck Lestat in general and I like this book because he's not in it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4125846359203852560" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_64220526" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64220526" />
    <a title="Natasha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2496802-natasha"><img alt="Natasha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572201679p2/2496802.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/64220526?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natasha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natasha" href="/user/show/2496802-natasha">Natasha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64220526" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17045292704039210810"><b>Vittorio: The Vampire</b> is the second novel in the New Tales of the Vampires series by the legendary Anne Rice. Honestly, I first read this novel a few years ago, but I fell in love with this story so much that I had to read it again. I've read some love and some hate reviews on this novel and honestly, I don't see why their would be any hate. Sure, everyone's opinions are welcome, but I personally think this novel turned me into a vampire lover. Yes, I know many will say, "Not her Vampire Chronic</span>
  <span id="freeText17045292704039210810" style="display:none"><b>Vittorio: The Vampire</b> is the second novel in the New Tales of the Vampires series by the legendary Anne Rice. Honestly, I first read this novel a few years ago, but I fell in love with this story so much that I had to read it again. I've read some love and some hate reviews on this novel and honestly, I don't see why their would be any hate. Sure, everyone's opinions are welcome, but I personally think this novel turned me into a vampire lover. Yes, I know many will say, "Not her Vampire Chronicles novels?? Come on!" Well, I admit, her Vampire Chronicles are fantastic and they truly are the heart of vampires. Although, I read Interview with the Vampire/Queen of the Damned much to young to appreciate it's greatness. Yes, I loved them, but what made me beg for more vampires and horror was Vittorio. I got this novel on a whim from my friend and boy am I glad he lent me this novel. Who knows how long it would have taken me to get into the amazing novels I so in love with now. <br /><br />Anyway, onto my thoughts on this novel. I truly believe there are many novels you can fall in love with. The characters, storyline and especially, the world that is created. I have so many novels I love for so many reasons, but honestly, I remember everything about this novel. The spot I read it, which was my bed and on the couch. (Take it in mind this was over 5 years ago) I remember being entranced in the world Anne Rice has created. Vittorio's pain was my pain, his joy was my joy and his interest was my own. <br /><br />Anne, as always describes this world in detail. I feel as if I'm right there next to Vittorio. Battling with him, crying with him and feeling the seduction he feels. It's truly a beautifully written novel.<br /><br />This is one of those novels I know I'll read for a third, or many even a fourth time, just to get involved in this world again. I really am disappointed there wasn't more novels in this series, but since I haven't read the first, I think I'll go back to finally read it. Why haven't I read it if I loev this one so much, you might ask? honestly, I loved this one so much, I don't want to be disappointed. I don't believe it will be a bad book, none of her vampire novels I've read are even close to being disappointing. I just love Vittorio so much, he's always going to be "my first". Everyone has their first. Who's yours??? </span>
  <a data-text-id="17045292704039210810" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_833013870" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/833013870" />
    <a title="Alex Reborn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10931679-alex-reborn"><img alt="Alex Reborn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461358532p2/10931679.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/833013870?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex Reborn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex Reborn" href="/user/show/10931679-alex-reborn">Alex Reborn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer833013870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12541187759913478004">The truth is that I really wanted to finish with all the Chronicles and "Vittorio" managed to convince me that I am right by doing just that. I barely managed to get through the entire book and very often I wanted to put it aside, and only my persistence kept me going. I think I got tired of the writing style, with the same descriptions and lack of engaging action. The mixing of the vampires and angels is a bit peculiar, for some it all falls in the supernatural category, but for me is a bad mix</span>
  <span id="freeText12541187759913478004" style="display:none">The truth is that I really wanted to finish with all the Chronicles and "Vittorio" managed to convince me that I am right by doing just that. I barely managed to get through the entire book and very often I wanted to put it aside, and only my persistence kept me going. I think I got tired of the writing style, with the same descriptions and lack of engaging action. The mixing of the vampires and angels is a bit peculiar, for some it all falls in the supernatural category, but for me is a bad mixture for this kind of book. It shows too much about the author, the questioning about religion, good and evil, angels, and I was left with the feeling that vampires were just stuffed in the tale. However, this time just didn't work for me and I'd rather keep the distance from now on. Moreover, there was some eroticism involved in the story which seemed awkward and wrong. <br /><br />Vittorio was really annoying, he kept talking and was quite slow in understanding the circumstances. Another thing I disliked was the fact that he just couldn't decide if he was fascinated by the vampires or if he considered them demons, if he was attracted or repugnant by them. I comprehend the compulsion, the feeling that you can't stop staring, but this was ridiculous. In my opinion, the story didn't really have a solid frame and by the end it just fell off. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12541187759913478004" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3308073239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10944249683967135367">Sorry to say this about Anne, but this is the most ridiculous books I’ve ever read. I can’t believe how such a garbage can could be written by the same person who did some amazing books I really loved. This was a disappointment. A huge one.<br/><br/>The dark, gothic, brutal, romantic atmosphere was nowhere to be found. There were attempts to create it but they were failures. Ursula and Florian were solely created to rouse that lustrous aroma but, boy it was just pathetic. Even the language was so sloppy a</span>
  <span id="freeText10944249683967135367" style="display:none">Sorry to say this about Anne, but this is the most ridiculous books I’ve ever read. I can’t believe how such a garbage can could be written by the same person who did some amazing books I really loved. This was a disappointment. A huge one.<br /><br />The dark, gothic, brutal, romantic atmosphere was nowhere to be found. There were attempts to create it but they were failures. Ursula and Florian were solely created to rouse that lustrous aroma but, boy it was just pathetic. Even the language was so sloppy and thin. <br /><br /><br />There’s a reason why the vampires and Satans clan was always kept apart. They’re glorious on their own. In this book everything is jumbled up and has become one lousy masala where vampires are black mass conducting disciples of satan and that made the whole thing comical &amp; stupid. Then there’s a bunch of angels too. This was one tiresome religious mumbo jumbo. <br /><br />It’s been a long time since I’ve read Anne Rice and I really hoped this would be worth it. I’m just so furious. She should’ve left her catholic faith and religion out of this. She could worship a cow for all I care but when it was poured out across 300 odd pages, it becomes a tiresome and a tasteless shitpile...<br /><br /><br /><i>2020 Poposugar reading challenge - A book by an author with flora or fauna in their name<br />Books in the time of Covid-19 #15<br />Book 32 of 2020</i></span>

<div id="review_159940765" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159940765" />
    <a title="Austin Neaves" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4681844-austin-neaves"><img alt="Austin Neaves" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353705626p2/4681844.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159940765?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Austin Neaves" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Austin Neaves" href="/user/show/4681844-austin-neaves">Austin Neaves</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4681844-austin-neaves?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159940765" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15972024070739023774">Vittorio the Vampire is the second (and final) book in the series "New Tales of the Vampires" by Anne Rice. It's different from the previous novel, Pandora. This novel has entirely original characters. Whereas Paganism played an important role in Pandora, Christianity is the focus in this novel.<br/><br/>And I think that's the part of the novel that shines. By this time in the series, the vampire thing is kind of old. I still enjoy the vampire aspect, but I found the angels in this book to be a refreshing</span>
  <span id="freeText15972024070739023774" style="display:none">Vittorio the Vampire is the second (and final) book in the series "New Tales of the Vampires" by Anne Rice. It's different from the previous novel, Pandora. This novel has entirely original characters. Whereas Paganism played an important role in Pandora, Christianity is the focus in this novel.<br /><br />And I think that's the part of the novel that shines. By this time in the series, the vampire thing is kind of old. I still enjoy the vampire aspect, but I found the angels in this book to be a refreshing and a complimentary addition to the "Anne Rice" take on vampires.<br /><br />Like all of Rice's novels, history and art are important to the story. This novel features the work of Fra Filippo Lippi, an artist during the time of Cosimo de' Medici, as well as the writings of Thomas Aquinas and St. Augustine. All of it flows effortlessly through the story, enriching the experience just as I've come to expect from a Rice novel.<br /><br />The novel is short (My hardcover was 288 pages) and it's a quick read (took me two days), but it's worth it. I think it's best to view this story on it's own. It's completely different from the other vampire books. I didn't find it to be better or worse - only different. And that's what makes it special. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15972024070739023774" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3877861037976413438">I probably got to page 43-50, and then started to jump around in the book, and decided to read the end of the book. Well the first couple chapters I was enjoying, when the character was talking about his about his life, but when his family was slaughtered, he goes out finding the Ursela, who had put the attack on his family, he finds her, is ready to take his revenge, blah blah blah, just to be made into a vampire, then falls in love with her. OKAY to me that is just weird, you fell in love with</span>
  <span id="freeText3877861037976413438" style="display:none">I probably got to page 43-50, and then started to jump around in the book, and decided to read the end of the book. Well the first couple chapters I was enjoying, when the character was talking about his about his life, but when his family was slaughtered, he goes out finding the Ursela, who had put the attack on his family, he finds her, is ready to take his revenge, blah blah blah, just to be made into a vampire, then falls in love with her. OKAY to me that is just weird, you fell in love with the same person who had slaughtered your family, yeah rather hard to believe, well it is for me anyway. <br /><br />Anne Rice obviously did her research for the book dating it back to Florence in the 1400's. The book itself was lacking in plot, and foreshadowing, probably a few other things as well. I understand that the character was supposed to be in conflict with himself for many different reason's, but to me they seemed rather contradictory despite her efforts in writing the character. </span>

It's an odd concept. The rest of the book? Convoluted and boring. </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375401602" href="/book/show/43824.Vittorio_the_Vampire">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of gothic horror</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16684387-bonnie?shelf=science-fiction-horror">science-fiction-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16684387-bonnie?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer560838608" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1883974138011549822">Strange and somewhat different in style than Anne Rice's usual vampire writing. This means that it was exciting wondering what horror was going to unfold next, but the character was not full of passion and wonder and dear to my heart the way her Vampire Chronicles characters are. But I think Anne Rice meant for it to be that way; seems she just wanted to get out of her comfort zone.<br/><br/>My biggest problem with this story was the repetition of each of her vampires: why do they all have to come from we</span>
  <span id="freeText1883974138011549822" style="display:none">Strange and somewhat different in style than Anne Rice's usual vampire writing. This means that it was exciting wondering what horror was going to unfold next, but the character was not full of passion and wonder and dear to my heart the way her Vampire Chronicles characters are. But I think Anne Rice meant for it to be that way; seems she just wanted to get out of her comfort zone.<br /><br />My biggest problem with this story was the repetition of each of her vampires: why do they all have to come from wealthy, if not royal, backgrounds? No beautiful homeless youths for an older vampire to fall in love with? And secondly, why do they all have to reflect her Roman Catholic views (even the pre-Christian vampires, to some extent)? You're telling me none of the vampires can be Lutheran or something? What are the odds?<br /><br />In any case, I still had some fun with the book, and I think maybe if I had read this by any other author, I might have felt better about it.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_116969080" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/116969080" />
    <a title="Mayara Arend" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3980722-mayara-arend"><img alt="Mayara Arend" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285254436p2/3980722.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/116969080?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mayara Arend" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mayara Arend" href="/user/show/3980722-mayara-arend">Mayara Arend</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer116969080&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer116969080" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6378951157704870213">Whoever knows Anne Rice, knows they can only expect one thing from her: Surprise.<br/><br/><br/>Despite her several books about vampires, each character is completelly unique, with different characteristics, fears and powers.<br/><br/>Vittorio is another one of them. Even though he's similar, on some points, to Louis (from Interview with a Vampire), he has a much more warrior-like disposition, because, unlike Louis, Vittorio was born during the Italian Renaissance period, being educated as a knight, to protect his land.</span>
  <span id="freeText6378951157704870213" style="display:none">Whoever knows Anne Rice, knows they can only expect one thing from her: Surprise.<br /><br /><br />Despite her several books about vampires, each character is completelly unique, with different characteristics, fears and powers.<br /><br />Vittorio is another one of them. Even though he's similar, on some points, to Louis (from Interview with a Vampire), he has a much more warrior-like disposition, because, unlike Louis, Vittorio was born during the Italian Renaissance period, being educated as a knight, to protect his land.<br /><br />The story starts telling about Vittorio's life and his family, who owns some land in Italy, in which several families live, protected by Vittorio's father.<br /><br />Some vampires show up and propose that they handle to them the children, old and sick, people no one would miss, to them, but Vittorio's father refuses and that causes the death of all his family except, of course, our main character, whose life is saved by Ursula, a beautiful and seductive vampire.<br /><br />That's when the hunt starts: Vittorio wants revenge for his family, because their deaths made him shocked and unsettled, but, at the same time, starts Ursula's hunt to Vittorio, who, obviously, saved him for a reason.<br /><br />Well, I'm not telling the whole story here. Of course we know that Vittorio becomes a vampire or that wouldn't be the title of the book (at least in Brazil that's the title), but what I liked, specially, was that we didn't know WHEN it was going to happen! Each moment, each part of the story, we are caught wondering "is it now?".<br /><br />There are beautiful parts, conversations with angels, beautiful descriptions of the paintings Vittorio loves so much, of the Rubi Graarl Court (hopefully the English name is the same), of Ursula. But also there are parts extremelly irritating, where we think "STOP, DON'T DO THAT", because we know exactly what's going to happen - even though he doesn't see it.<br /><br />Do not expect a "Twilight" love: Vittorio and Ursula love eachother on a passionate, physical, sad, full of guilt way, after all, she did help to kill his family. After Vittorio is changed, he, unlike Louis menioned above, understands his new situation and accepts it - it's irremediable, and his love for Ursula keeps him alive.<br /><br />It's a wonderful book, exciting and different from most vampire books you've read, that talks about love and hate, of how close they can be and how can someone be, at the same time, full of hate and completelly good, innocent and benevolent.<br /><br />After "the tale of the Body thief" I thought Anne Rice had lost it, because Lestat was incredibly boring, sounding more like a dumb Superman and the story was very weak, but with Vittorio, you see clearly it wasn't her, but Lestat that had lost it and me who "had enough of him".<br /><br />@<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://brazilianbookworm.blogspot.com/">http://brazilianbookworm.blogspot.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6378951157704870213" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer700247441" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer908229789998003502">Some years ago I read the Mayfair Witches series and I really enjoyed it. So, why not read one of Anne Rice´s vampire books? Big mistake! This book was a total disappointment. <br/>Vittorio, son of a rich lord, sees his family slaughtered by a group of vampires and only escapes because a female vampire, Ursula, thinks him extremely attractive. Vittorio swears vengeance and with the help of a group of guardian angels, sets out to kill the sons of the devil. But the growing fascination he feels for Urs</span>
  <span id="freeText908229789998003502" style="display:none">Some years ago I read the Mayfair Witches series and I really enjoyed it. So, why not read one of Anne Rice´s vampire books? Big mistake! This book was a total disappointment. <br />Vittorio, son of a rich lord, sees his family slaughtered by a group of vampires and only escapes because a female vampire, Ursula, thinks him extremely attractive. Vittorio swears vengeance and with the help of a group of guardian angels, sets out to kill the sons of the devil. But the growing fascination he feels for Ursula doesn´t make his mission easy…<br />I think this book lacked rhythm. It was very slow sometimes and I got a bit fed up with Vittorio´s grieving and weeping and going on and on and on about his revenge. It was very tiresome. And the scenes with the angels were just childish. The best part of the book was the setting, which Anne Rice paints in very vivid colours – the vampire den, the monasteries, the renascence towns - and I also liked the references to Fra Filippo´s life and works. Historical notes apart, this book was a total bore.<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText2098625665728465060" style="display:none">It is my least favorite Anne Rice, because it takes place in the 17th Century. It is magnificent. There are no werewolves with these vampires; but there are Angels. It has all the Anne Rice characteristics of Good and Evil, Blood, Sex and Love. It is written in the formal style of speaking at that time in history. And also includes the ignorance, violence and prejudices of the time. Showing that she did alot of research for the story, at the end of the book, in addition to her usual Note on the Type, she includes a Selected and Annotated Bibliography. I prefer her novels that take place in New Orleans; this takes place in Florence. Both the type and the Bib are Italian. She says you really have to go to both New Orleans and Florence to understand their similarities; both cities of "public spectacles, rituals, and feast days, of demonstrations of communal celebration and belief."</span>

<div id="review_146970282" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/146970282" />
    <a title="David Gillis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4835089-david-gillis"><img alt="David Gillis" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/146970282?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Gillis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Gillis" href="/user/show/4835089-david-gillis">David Gillis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer146970282" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9191545612644084297">I found that this novel was a bit of a disappointment. On the one hand, Vittorio is a deep character with enough angst coursing through his body he could put Edward Cullen to shame. Vittorio is angry, lustful, depressed, and confused as he moves throughout the story, and Rice manages to capture that rather well. However, many of the scenes are described rather dreamily. This could be on purpose, as Ursula seduces Vittorio, and we the readers are taken along for the ride. If so, then it is an int</span>
  <span id="freeText9191545612644084297" style="display:none">I found that this novel was a bit of a disappointment. On the one hand, Vittorio is a deep character with enough angst coursing through his body he could put Edward Cullen to shame. Vittorio is angry, lustful, depressed, and confused as he moves throughout the story, and Rice manages to capture that rather well. However, many of the scenes are described rather dreamily. This could be on purpose, as Ursula seduces Vittorio, and we the readers are taken along for the ride. If so, then it is an interesting technique that has a lot to offer. However, given how slow the pace is throughout the story, trying to actually get with the plot is a struggle because of this affect. Furthermore, I think that the novel suffers from the amount of angst Vittorio goes through, especially because of how slow the story can seem at times. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9191545612644084297" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leslie Wiederspan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leslie Wiederspan" href="/user/show/18142405-leslie-wiederspan">Leslie Wiederspan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer943890841" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13104247800339755167">I thought this book was going to be like "Pandora". In a way, i was. It's the story of how Vittorio first became a vampire. But, I didnt like it. For starters, he is a 16 year old boy and she makes it seem like he is a knowledgeable man, fully grown. I get it, back in the 1400's boys were stronger and were taught in the ways of Lordly ways and war. But Vittorio is 16. I find this story really hard to believe. Oh, and throw in the gaurdian angels and the constant referenced to Christianity. This </span>
  <span id="freeText13104247800339755167" style="display:none">I thought this book was going to be like "Pandora". In a way, i was. It's the story of how Vittorio first became a vampire. But, I didnt like it. For starters, he is a 16 year old boy and she makes it seem like he is a knowledgeable man, fully grown. I get it, back in the 1400's boys were stronger and were taught in the ways of Lordly ways and war. But Vittorio is 16. I find this story really hard to believe. Oh, and throw in the gaurdian angels and the constant referenced to Christianity. This was an easy read, but I found it very difficult to finish. A 16 year old who knows more about the world than those adults around him, every other sentence seemed to be a reference to Christ, God, Jesus etc., angels are everywhere and help him, he falls in love immediately with a vampire, and he has the strength of a hardened soldier, makes this book, well, ridiculous. Very disappointing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13104247800339755167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1476156253" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1476156253" />
    <a title="Sissy Lu {Book Savvy Reviews}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17779484-sissy-lu-book-savvy-reviews"><img alt="Sissy Lu {Book Savvy Reviews}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541599657p2/17779484.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1476156253?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sissy Lu {Book Savvy Reviews}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sissy Lu {Book Savvy Reviews}" href="/user/show/17779484-sissy-lu-book-savvy-reviews">Sissy Lu {Book Savvy Reviews}</a>
      </span>

          marked it as dnf


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345439321" href="/book/show/1135482.Vittorio_the_Vampire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17779484-sissy-lu-book-savvy-reviews?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1476156253" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8088543576943502068">For me it is always a hit or miss with Anne Rice. This one was a miss. When she was actually writing about the <i>actual</i> story that was relevant I was intrigued, but the way it was written in a rampant fashion that often became sidetracked and the narrator [Vittorio] constantly had to check himself to get back on track, it was distracting and kept me from engaging as well as becoming invested in him and his story. <br/><br/>I DNF at 60 mark or so. Too many books on my list to MAKE myself read something!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17830025-kathleen?shelf=best-books-ever">best-books-ever</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer856902991" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14539578387841709907">So I am done with all of Anne Rice’s vampire novels. All twelve. It was kind of hard to keep reading in some spots, like Merrick and Memnoch the Devil, but I managed it. Vittorio…the second of Rice’s New Tales of the Vampires, the spin-off series. Apparently the second and also the last, since she hasn’t touched it since this one in 1999. So this was written right after The Vampire Armand and obviously Rice was going through a Renaissance phase, since Armand took place during the High Renaissanc</span>
  <span id="freeText14539578387841709907" style="display:none">So I am done with all of Anne Rice’s vampire novels. All twelve. It was kind of hard to keep reading in some spots, like Merrick and Memnoch the Devil, but I managed it. Vittorio…the second of Rice’s New Tales of the Vampires, the spin-off series. Apparently the second and also the last, since she hasn’t touched it since this one in 1999. So this was written right after The Vampire Armand and obviously Rice was going through a Renaissance phase, since Armand took place during the High Renaissance and this is the Early Renaissance. So the artwork the main character happens to love is not as good as in Armand, but whatever. <br />So the entire book is Vittorio’s origin story, like Pandora and most of the Vampire Chronicles. I guess I can see why Rice got bored with this series and stopped writing for a decade. I mean, she was just going through each vampire’s story from the middle to the end of the series, until the last book where she had to tie things up. <br />I didn’t think I would like this book. It was just the last step in my vampiric Rice journey. I was excited for Pandora, which turned out to just be okay and I was dreading this one and didn’t know what to expect. But it was amazing! <br />Vittorio starts off the book by saying there is no connection between him and Lestat’s vampires in the Chronicles. Which was weird for me. I had no idea where it was going.<br />Vittorio is a rich son of a lord and his family is killed when his father pissed off the leader of the local vampire coven. I wish they got more into that, being the first out of my two complaints, though they mentioned it again, but it was too brief for my taste. So Vittorio kind of falls in love with one of his attackers, a girl vampire named Ursula. She lets him go, but the rest of his family is dead. So he swears vengeance and leaves for the town of Santa Maddalana, not really planning it, he just kind of wanders in grief somewhere. So the town is oddly happy and prosperous and Vittorio likes that for a while. But he soon discovers that the town has been offering its “undesirable” occupants to the vampire coven to the north in the mountains. Vittorio hides out in an abandoned castle where he is captured by a vampire who takes him back to their lair. Vittorio actually manages to kill the vampire and Ursula begs for his life and for him to be transformed as well. Vittorio mouths off to the coven leader, Florian, and is sent to live with the captured people about to be drained of blood. Then they drag him to a blood ritual church ceremony when they worship Satan and kill people. Vittorio rejects the offer of the immortal blood and is dumped, poisoned with vampiric blood and kind of crazy, in Florence. He is taken in by an order of monks, but not before he sees three angels, the guardians of the artist he loves, Filippo Lippi. I was completely surprised at this. Rice has never mentioned angels before in her series. This book felt completely different from her other vampire books, though it had a similar message. The angels and Vittorio’s conversations with them were really interesting. It made me want to read Songs of the Seraphim, her newer series about angels. So the angels agree to help Vittorio kill the vampire coven, even though they did not get precise orders from God to do so. Vittorio swears to kill all the vampires, including Ursula. <br />I kind of liked how the vampires wandered the earth forever, wondering if there was a higher power, and that is not really here with Vittorio. Vittorio describes the vampires in Biblical terms, which makes sense because of the time period he comes from. We kind of get “proof” of God, but I didn’t mind it too much because all the angels we met were unique and the dialogue was very well done. So that was my second compliant and neither of those were actually a big deal for me. I loved this book. <br />So Vittorio slays all the vampires during the day with some help from the angels in a gore-fest with lots of detailed imagery. But he cannot slay Ursula and instead waits beside her until she wakes up at nightfall. The angels leave, disgusted that he broke his promise. Ursula then tricks Vittorio into becoming a vampire too, which I think he totally should have seen coming. Together, they kill off all the evil villagers in Santa Maddalana. Vittorio likes living and is too fearful of Hell to destroy himself as he knows he should, so he continues to live in sin with Ursula. They depart for Florence (more food there) and hear the news that Filippo Lippi is in huge trouble because he ran off with a nun the day that his guardian angels went to help Vittorio. They go to Filippo’s house and the angels there are angry at him for not keeping his promise and becoming a murderer. The lead angel curses him with the ability to see the divine spark of Creation in every living being, like an angel, so that when Vittorio kills, he will be haunted by the sight of the spark going out. The angels leave and Vittorio is horrified. <br />This really drives home the theme Rice loves to write about (and I love to read), that the vampires hate killing, but must kill to live, and begin to detest themselves (though some like Marius, justify it by killing the Evil Doer). Vittorio and Ursula return to Vittorio’s castle where he grew up and have been together for five hundred years (finally a vampire couple that actually stays together) and Vittorio is in self-torment. I love this ending! I loved this book! The suspense was great, the action was great, the dialogue (especially the angels). It was all great! This would be an amazing movie too! Though it felt a little disjointed from the tone and feel of the other vampire novels, I really enjoyed this one. It was surprising, heartfelt, poetic, and refreshing. I am so excited to continue reading Rice’s work and am thoroughly impressed. Definitely ended this series on a good note for me and I can’t wait to read The Prince Lestat in October! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14539578387841709907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Elise" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3982733-elise"><img alt="Elise" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506049008p2/3982733.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1598642423?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elise" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elise" href="/user/show/3982733-elise">Elise</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345422392" href="/book/show/159451.Vittorio_the_Vampire">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1598642423" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6022658844483856818">It hurts me to give this book a 2 star rating.<br/><br/>I love most of Anne Rice's stories, so it sucks that this one wasn't that great. I loved the first 2 chapters of this book. It started out pretty nice and strong. It had a great opening paragraph, where Vittorio describes holding his brother and sisters' severed heads in his arms. And I was like, fuck yeah! This is gonna be some good shit. But it wasn't. It really wasn't. Because then it just went nose diving downhill. I hate Anne Rice's tendency to </span>
  <span id="freeText6022658844483856818" style="display:none">It hurts me to give this book a 2 star rating.<br /><br />I love most of Anne Rice's stories, so it sucks that this one wasn't that great. I loved the first 2 chapters of this book. It started out pretty nice and strong. It had a great opening paragraph, where Vittorio describes holding his brother and sisters' severed heads in his arms. And I was like, fuck yeah! This is gonna be some good shit. But it wasn't. It really wasn't. Because then it just went nose diving downhill. I hate Anne Rice's tendency to bring in God/the Devil/Angels/Heaven/Hell/Christian mythology into her stories. I never read those kind of stories, I'm not religious and I do. not. give. a. shit. Now, sometimes she touches on those themes in other books but leaves them alone and gets on with a good story. I'm ok with that. But I'm not ok with it when she goes on and on and on about angels. Like, Vittorio, pull yourself together. Drink some blood, live forever. Stop whining. So it hurts me to give this book a 2 star rating when I usually thoroughly enjoy her books.<br /><br />In reality, this is really a 1 star read. I found it incredibly dull and I struggled to make it through. <br />The reason I decided on 2 stars instead of 1 is because Anne Rice is still a beautiful writer, and because I have read and enjoyed so many of her other books. I still have to read the Lives of the Mayfair Witches book so here's hoping she kinda eases up on the religious motifs a bit. And if not....well, it breaks my heart to even consider the implications of 'if not'.<br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_960644912" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/960644912" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/960644912?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joshua" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joshua" href="/user/show/7810047-joshua">Joshua</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7810047-joshua?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7810047-joshua?shelf=fiction-faves">fiction-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7810047-joshua?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer960644912" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16827540152215225869">Vittorio the Vampire presents a differing picture of vampires than what Anne has presented with her seminal Vampire Chronicles Series (which I'm slowly working through). <br/><br/>The story begins with young Vittorio and his family living in regal elegance in Lordship over the hamlets and farmland of their valley located somewhere in Italy within proximity of Florence. The story quickly escalates taking the reader on a harrowing journey. <br/><br/>I don't want to say too much ruining the story, but Vittorio becomes</span>
  <span id="freeText16827540152215225869" style="display:none">Vittorio the Vampire presents a differing picture of vampires than what Anne has presented with her seminal Vampire Chronicles Series (which I'm slowly working through). <br /><br />The story begins with young Vittorio and his family living in regal elegance in Lordship over the hamlets and farmland of their valley located somewhere in Italy within proximity of Florence. The story quickly escalates taking the reader on a harrowing journey. <br /><br />I don't want to say too much ruining the story, but Vittorio becomes enraptured with a vampire woman, Ursala who he falls madly in love with. Her toothy bite disposing him to unparalleled rapture and ecstasy. It's also a story of faith for young Vittorio grapples with his deep draw and feelings towards a demon and his own Christian faith. The vampires themselves in this novel are of a decidedly Satanic and ritualistic variety. Eventually Vittorio decides he must seek out and destroy these creatures of the night, but has to come to terms with potentially having to destroy Ursala the creature he is so drawn to by "love." Angels come to Vittorio's aide about half way through the novel coming as a complete surprise to me. <br /><br />Basically it's a story of good and evil and the young man coming to terms with the fact that people and life isn't always so black and white. Definitely a good read, written in Anne Rice's usual descriptive and beautiful prose. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16827540152215225869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1451552159311755204">i cannot believe that this is from anne rice. o.O i love all the books of the vampire chronicles! i have read lestat, interview, queen, blood and gold and pandora. all of them were marvelous. so it was a mere shock to read this one. most of the book is too religious for me, i have to admit that. i didn't like the emphasis on it. also the short span of time that is told annoys me greatly. there is nothing interesting in it! it is how vittorio was made, that is all. also the vampires are so unlike</span>
  <span id="freeText1451552159311755204" style="display:none">i cannot believe that this is from anne rice. o.O i love all the books of the vampire chronicles! i have read lestat, interview, queen, blood and gold and pandora. all of them were marvelous. so it was a mere shock to read this one. most of the book is too religious for me, i have to admit that. i didn't like the emphasis on it. also the short span of time that is told annoys me greatly. there is nothing interesting in it! it is how vittorio was made, that is all. also the vampires are so unlike rice's vampires. they are truly only demons. there is nothing of the depth of characters as in the other books. i simply don't care about those characters! it also bugged the hell out of me that vittorio, the oh so rightly, just and whatever human suddenly forgets all about this and goes rampaging with his beloved. no remorse there, right? this was ridiculous. also the golden halo is just mentioned in the end. it's so anticlimatic. this is basically the thing he suffers from, but he does not seem to suffer at all? i do not get the sense of it. i would have given only one star, but the second one is for the angels. i did like them and i loved them as characters. it's a shame they don't appear in other books. </span>

<div id="review_294605295" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/294605295" />
    <a title="Audrie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3567400-audrie"><img alt="Audrie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577769356p2/3567400.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/294605295?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Audrie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Audrie" href="/user/show/3567400-audrie">Audrie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer294605295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15089926895203965469">I just didn't like it as much as the original vampires. I missed the original characters, honestly. It just didn't feel complete without them, and I was almost expecting them all to appear behind every page. Sure, Vittorio was a good character, and the part about the angels was fascinating...but this book went more mature than my previous reads with Rice (Other than this one I've only read Queen of the Damned and The Vampire Lestat) and this is my personal taste...but I just wasn't a fan. Sure, </span>
  <span id="freeText15089926895203965469" style="display:none">I just didn't like it as much as the original vampires. I missed the original characters, honestly. It just didn't feel complete without them, and I was almost expecting them all to appear behind every page. Sure, Vittorio was a good character, and the part about the angels was fascinating...but this book went more mature than my previous reads with Rice (Other than this one I've only read Queen of the Damned and The Vampire Lestat) and this is my personal taste...but I just wasn't a fan. Sure, let them sex it up. It didn't really make sense at that point in their "relationship" but I suppose Ursula can do whatever she wants. That doesn't bother me all that much. It's just...I don't want to get a description as in-depth as this book gave me. I'm not a smut-novel fan and I was really worried that this book was going to turn into one. Give me biting and maiming any day...just keep the smut in its own genre.<br /><br /><br /><br />((This book did not turn into a devastatingly smutty novel. It, truth be told, kept itself very respectable. It was just too close for my personal comfort zone. Romance is whatever, just keep the private life private.))</span>
  <a data-text-id="15089926895203965469" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_471428659" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/471428659" />
    <a title="Dorian Jandreau" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15202946-dorian-jandreau"><img alt="Dorian Jandreau" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546633695p2/15202946.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/471428659?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dorian Jandreau" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dorian Jandreau" href="/user/show/15202946-dorian-jandreau">Dorian Jandreau</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099271093" href="/book/show/1178822.Vittorio_the_Vampire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15202946-dorian-jandreau?shelf=my-biggest-treasures">my-biggest-treasures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15202946-dorian-jandreau?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15202946-dorian-jandreau?shelf=beloved-anne-rice">beloved-anne-rice</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer471428659" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9306502315656486514">First it was very boring book. I don't know why. I left it for a while away while I was in Italy. When When I came back from Italy, I started reading this again and felt a different spirit for this book. It became interesting to me. Of course, my interest changed because I visited Florence and when I came back home, this book became easier for me to read, because I already was in that city where Vittorio was. It was easier to imagine scenes and revive my travel's memories. Of course, I had just </span>
  <span id="freeText9306502315656486514" style="display:none">First it was very boring book. I don't know why. I left it for a while away while I was in Italy. When When I came back from Italy, I started reading this again and felt a different spirit for this book. It became interesting to me. Of course, my interest changed because I visited Florence and when I came back home, this book became easier for me to read, because I already was in that city where Vittorio was. It was easier to imagine scenes and revive my travel's memories. Of course, I had just few hours in Florence, it was already an evening, but I saw what made me... crazed. I was crying like mad in Florence because of art I saw, so I can understand why Vittorio so adored the art he saw in Florence. It is very hard to describe such art, but Anne Rice did this well in this book. <br /><br />Maybe some scenes were boring a little bit. I get bored easily if I need to read about nature, weather and something like that. But in the end of the book, things changed. I was happy to read interesting tale. If I had to tell in one word what I think of this book, I would say "ARTISTIC". Rich in art, culture and history. It warmed my heart and soul.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9306502315656486514" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Nk626UZalaBwOIeT4bNOajupIiNuvagKBxCkIqLCHKRR1pyq7r1moS2ybg7Xp7LKGE5WP2FXImRhuQhg/IYPBA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5QIOZwi+PEg52FxiCUi85wQWQFTp+yDCyDNJBVdZiQyCmiQkoFnPSWRStf8/XEBHJ/E0SOYRqqyumuVHCR2arA==')})
  }

For Britain had not just lost a prince: during his twenty year marriage to Queen Victoria, Prince Albert had increasingly performed the function of King in all but name. The outpouring of grief after Albert\'s death was so extreme, that its like would not be seen again until the death of Princess Diana 136 years later.\n\nDrawing on many letters, diaries and memoirs from the Royal Archives and other neglected sources, as well as the newspapers of the day, Rappaport offers a new perspective on this compelling historical psychodrama--the crucial final months of the prince\'s life and the first long, dark ten years of the Queen\'s retreat from public view. She draws a portrait of a queen obsessed with her living husband and - after his death - with his enduring place in history. This book is for guitarists who are curious to find out what is inside a fuzz, overdrive, octave or amp-in-a-box pedal, and how manufacturers select the options available in the circuit to get just the right combination of tones. It is an essential guide to distortion stompboxes, and explains the many circuit variations being used today.  Since the early days of the electric guitar, the selection of fuzz and distortion pedals has greatly expanded and new models are being introduced every month. Most pedal manufacturers have numerous versions in their product lines.  Written in a conversational style that should appeal to DIY Makers, hobbyists and guitarists who are just interested in what makes those hard-driving sounds, this book explains the technology of distortion and fuzz pedals in easy to understand language, with only a small amount of math and scientific jargon. Are you ready to delve into the mystery of those colorful boxes on the floor? You don\'t have to be an engineer to enjoy the book, so let’s begin! <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15108694535134142680">Anne Rice (born Howard Allen Frances O'Brien) is a best-selling American author of gothic, supernatural, historical, erotica, and later religious themed books. Best known for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&query=The+Vampire+Chronicles' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Vampire Chronicles</a>, her prevailing thematical focus is on love, death, immortality, existentialism, and the human condition. She was married to poet <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/222961.Stan_Rice' title='Stan Rice' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stan Rice</a> for 41 years until his death in 2002. Her books have sold near</span>
  <span id="freeText15108694535134142680" style="display:none">Anne Rice (born Howard Allen Frances O'Brien) is a best-selling American author of gothic, supernatural, historical, erotica, and later religious themed books. Best known for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&amp;query=The+Vampire+Chronicles" rel="nofollow noopener">The Vampire Chronicles</a>, her prevailing thematical focus is on love, death, immortality, existentialism, and the human condition. She was married to poet <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/222961.Stan_Rice" title="Stan Rice" rel="nofollow noopener">Stan Rice</a> for 41 years until his death in 2002. Her books have sold nearly 100 million copies, making her one of the most widely read authors in modern history.<br /><br />She uses the pseudonym <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17553.Anne_Rampling" rel="nofollow noopener">Anne Rampling</a> for adult-themed fiction (i.e., erotica) and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/437669.A_N_Roquelaure" rel="nofollow noopener">A.N. Roquelaure</a> for fiction featuring sexually explicit sado-masochism.</span>

She is two thousand years old, a Child of the Millennia, the first vampire ever made by the great Marius. David persuades her to tell the story of her life. \n\nPandora begins, reluctantly at first and then with increasing passion, to recount her mesmerizing tale, which takes us through the ages, from Imperial Rome to eighteenth-century France to twentieth-century Paris and New Orleans. She carries us back to her mortal girlhood in the world of Caesar Augustus, a world chronicled by Ovid and Petronius. This is where Pandora meets and falls in love with the handsome, charismatic, lighthearted, still-mortal Marius. This is the Rome she is forced to flee in fear of assassination by conspirators plotting to take over the city. And we follow her to the exotic port of Antioch, where she is destined to be reunited with Marius, now immortal and haunted by his vampire nature, who will bestow on her the Dark Gift as they set out
